Free Talk

A Word of Wisdom 224

— Li Long

If X-rays could illuminate people's hearts, the wicked of the world would surely be completely eliminated.

Waves rise without wind only in the sea of love.

The saying "A distant relative is not as good as a close neighbor" is not applicable in Shanghai because neighbors in Shanghai mostly do not know each other and cannot get to know each other.

If a person about to commit suicide could think that they are not afraid of death, what else is there to be afraid of? Perhaps they could actively pursue a career.

If a person's thoughts are too dull, it is indeed not good, but being too sensitive is also harmful.

Treat people with sincerity, and even if you don't get their favor, you won't make them resentful.

Today's young men and women only know how to seek partners, but not how to choose them, so successes are few and failures are many.

Only a mother's love for her child is the most genuine in the world, but people will not appreciate a mother's kindness until they are in dire straits.

Only clever men and women can use the word "love" as a tool for swindling money and hunting for pleasure, so those who sacrifice for love are all fools.

Illness enters through the mouth, and misfortune comes out of it. Therefore, the ancients used the metaphor of guarding the mouth like a bottle.

Visiting Treasures at Da Bao Ji 225

— Ke Dingjin

Yesterday afternoon, my old friend Wang Yiming came to see me, accompanied by three people who said they were from the Xiang River. They were uneasy about the banditry in their hometown and came to Shanghai to seek a peaceful life. They brought with them a true copy of the Lanting Xu preface from the Dingwu period. I once saw Sang Shichang's Lanting Examination, which stated, "Emperor Taizong of Tang obtained the true copy of Lanting and had it engraved at the Academy of Scholars. Zhu Liang usurped it and transported it to Bian capital. Yelü Deguang broke the Later Jin and carried this engraving across the river. After Emperor Taizong returned, he discarded it in the Slaughter Tiger Forest along with his luggage. Later, it was placed in Dingzhou. Hence, it was named Ding Ben, and the world called it the Dingwu Lanting, because Dingzhou was originally the Yiwu Army during the Tang Dynasty. During the Song Dynasty, to avoid the taboo of Emperor Taizong's name, it was renamed Dingwu. During the Ninghe period, the emperor ordered the former staff of the Dingwu school to inquire about the Lanting stone. They obtained it from Xue Sichang, a commander in Chang'an. At that time, Liang Shicheng, an eunuch and receiver in Chang'an, issued a decree to take the old engraving. Xue Sichang hastily made a rubbing of the stone with three sheets of paper. The first rubbing was dark, the second was light, and the third was even lighter. The world called it the cicada wing copy." Furthermore, Gengzi Xiaoxia Ji also says, "Sun Chengzhe also said that there are two types of Dingwu copies circulating in the world: fat and thin." What I saw this year was a scroll several zhang long, with clear handwriting. I have no doubt that it was the true copy of Dingwu. The sages who participated in the spring purification ceremony were also depicted on the scroll, with vivid expressions and exquisite workmanship. Each had a small biography attached, which was extremely elegant. It was truly a rare treasure in the world. Huang Tingjian's horizontal scroll, full of vigor and vitality, was complete in spirit. My friend Meng Weng Shouzhi likes to write in the style of Shangu, and recently, his "Lotus Sutra" calligraphy has been circulating. His brushwork is powerful and can be compared to Shangu. Youren wrote in the postscript, "Shangu would also nod in approval if he were alive again." This is no exaggeration. Meng Weng should be very happy to see this scroll. Four framed calligraphy scrolls written by He Shaoji and Zeng Guofan during the Qing Dynasty, a vertical axis of Wang Weiren, the top scholar during the Qianlong period, titled "Autumn Water Floats Golden Goose," were all excellent. A bronze plate unearthed at the same time as the Shang tripod was shaped like an old-fashioned copper basin. Although there were broken holes, when struck, it made a golden sound, which was strange. (It is said that a foreign company has purchased the Shang tripod for over 20,000 yuan.) There were knife marks on it that shone like gold, which was dazzling. I don't know what dynasty it was from. It is a pity that the bronze mirror from the Tang Dynasty was broken into two pieces. It is said that when a person looks at it at a high place, he can see the scenery dozens of miles away without any errors. The mirror surface is mottled with green flowers, and the color is elegant and simple. It is an ancient telescope. A piece of carnelian jade in the shape of a turtle shell and small. When viewed against the light, there are clear pine needles. It is like an elaborate painting. All of these are truly rare treasures in the world. I am rushing to write a letter to Huang Binhong and Zhang Shanzi to evaluate them. I unintentionally had the opportunity to visit them. My eyes were blessed immeasurably. The owner is Mr. Li from Xiangjiang, whose ancestors were colleagues and friends with Zeng Guofan.

Record of a Visit to Qishan 226

— Zhou Cailiang

Qishan is a famous scenic spot in Jin County. It is said that Emperor Qinshihuang of Qin once stayed here during his southern tour. It is about two li away from my town (Zhangxi), which is also the location of Mr. Gao Chuiwan's Keli. Every year, on the 1st and 28th of March of the lunar calendar and the 1st of April, there is a farmers' market. Those who come as scheduled, no matter how far, are crowded with each other, and trade is quite prosperous. Only after noon does it become quiet. It still follows the ancient system of having markets during the day. The other day, I happened to return home for business, and it happened to be the last time for this year's market. I knew that the opportunity could not be missed, so I went on foot after getting up in the morning. Walking and walking again, I arrived in less than half an hour. Along the way, bamboo fences and thatched houses made for a pleasant scenery, which was enough to refresh the spirits of those who have been trapped in the city for a long time. When I arrived at the foot of the mountain, I saw a sea of people, shoulder to shoulder. There was a sense of being on the book-covered road. In total, there were about 200 stalls on both sides. There was almost no space on the whole mountain. Looking at what was on display, most of it was agricultural tools. Unfortunately, they still clung to the old methods. It is lamentable that the progress of China's agricultural industry has not improved. Then I went up the steps, walking three times before reaching the top of the mountain. There was an ancient temple at the top. The temple had only three rooms, but the environment was quite clear and open. I went inside to rest for a while. As soon as I sat down, I suddenly saw what was called crooked poems on the wall, which were almost completely covered. Elegant and vulgar were mixed together, which was quite amusing to read. I don't know who started this bad habit of tarnishing famous scenic spots. As the saying goes, famous soil is not worth half a cent. It is true. Then I said goodbye and left. Suddenly, it started raining. I went straight to the pavilion at the foot of the mountain to take shelter. At that time, more and more people gathered with me. Soon, it was full. The pavilion was newly built. There was a couplet, "It is most regrettable that we are like drifting duckweeds passing by, unable to break off willows to give to travelers." The language is profound, which is enough to make us travelers feel alarmed. After a while, the rain stopped, and the farmers' market also came to an end. I then said that I would return and write this record.

Novel Scam 227

— Liu Mengdie

In Dongting Town, Xizhi, there is a Mr. Hua, a descendant of Grand Master Hongshan from the Three Smiles Play. His daughter married to Changan Town, thirty li away. She already had a son. One afternoon, the daughter saw a certain Jia from Dongting Town arrive breathlessly, saying, "Your father suddenly became critically ill last night in the middle of the night. He was treated too late, and he died at dawn. I have come to report the funeral." The daughter was shocked to hear this and almost fainted. Jia then continued, "Your mother said that the fortune teller has determined that the coffin will be placed at midnight tonight. She ordered you to return in a sedan chair. All the clothes and belongings that are inconvenient to carry in the chair can be packed up and given to me to take back first. The road is long at dusk, so hurry up!" The daughter thought that what he said made sense. She hurriedly arranged things in her boudoir. Thinking that she would have to stay for many days, she prepared enough clothes, shoes, and jewelry, forming a large package. After that, she thought that Jia had been in and out of her mother's house and seemed familiar, so she did not suspect him. She gave the package to him, and he left. Then, the daughter asked someone to prepare a sedan chair and hugged her son into it. She wept all the way. When she arrived home, it was already dark. She got out of the chair and entered the door, immediately crying loudly and calling for her father. Her father heard the sound in the inner room and came out in surprise to ask what was wrong. Her family also gathered in surprise. The daughter was even more surprised to see her father. Then she learned that her father was unharmed. She wiped away her tears and smiled, turning grief into joy, as if she did not care about the loss of her clothes and belongings. However, her father was very angry. He ordered people to search the market for Jia, but he had disappeared without a trace. It turned out that Jia was a strong member of the Red Pill Party. He had been without food for three days. He had a unique idea to relieve his worries. However, it was a very bad joke.

Success After Resentment 228

— Rooster Crest

The other day, at a friend's banquet, I heard Mr. Zhou say that near the Confucius Temple, there were two restaurants, closely aligned and competing fiercely in business. According to those in the know, this contains a history of resentment, which is quite amusing to recount.

Initially, a resident of Ningbo named Jin often ate out for breakfast. One day, he went to a restaurant near the Confucius Temple for tea and snacks. The business was booming, and the waiters were very busy. After waiting for over an hour, the snacks he ordered still hadn't arrived. Jin became impatient and angrily questioned the waiter, who didn't back down and glared back, mocking him: "If you're not satisfied with the slow service and delayed food here, you might as well open your own restaurant, then you can order things as you please!" Feeling ridiculed by the cold words, Jin angrily left. Unexpectedly, several months later, a new restaurant opened nearby, selling the same Yangzhou-style snacks. The owner was none other than Jin, who had left in anger. After a year of business, his livelihood was quite good, surpassing the original restaurant. This was truly a gift from the waiter's provocation.

Furthermore, I once heard someone from my hometown say that on both sides of the Guan Yi River in Wuxing City, there were many ferry boats, providing access to Jin Po Lane and the front of Youwen Hall. There was a wealthy man named Wen in the city. One rainy day, he took a ferry, and, feeling it was too slow, he argued with the boatman. The boatman was also impolite and mocked him, saying, "If you want to go faster, you might as well build a bridge over the river!" He probably didn't know it was Mr. Wen and deliberately made things difficult for him. Later, the local area suddenly heard about a plan to build a bridge. The one in charge of the project was none other than Mr. Wen, who had been insulted by the boatman. The bridge was completed the year before last and named Qiao Liang. The ferry business was severely impacted, but pedestrians found it very convenient. Money is all-powerful. This is similar to the previous story, achieving the same result through different means. There's no other way to describe it but as success after resentment.

Art News: The three famous painters Zhao Banbo, Wu Ziding, and Ma Wanli are all masters of poetry, calligraphy, and painting. Those who obtain their works treasure them. They are holding a joint exhibition at the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association starting on the (13th) for three days. It is expected to be a grand occasion (Tai Shousheng)

Inspection of Breast Binding 229

— Talia

Since the custom of women binding their breasts became popular, people have followed suit, with no sign of decline. Although the Ministry of Interior has repeatedly issued orders to ban it, the speakers are earnest, but the listeners are indifferent. This is especially true among female students in schools. It is now heard that the Xiaoshan County Girls' Middle School in Zhejiang Province believes that breast binding is harmful to the health of female students and has ordered all female students to liberate their breasts and plans to conduct regular inspections to prevent concealment. As a result, the female students of the school have been looking ashamed these days.

The harm of breast binding to women is not only related to the health of the individual and postpartum fertility, but also has a profound impact, leading the nation to a state of weakness. Now, the school has pioneered liberation. The news has spread far and wide. It is not only pleasing to the women themselves but also a cause for celebration for the future of the nation.

Rotary Club Fiction

Three Eras (4) 230

— Zhang Henshui

(2) Sacrificed for Cornbread

By four o'clock in the afternoon, it was time for Zhang Xiaosan to return his rickshaw. He took the rickshaw back to the rickshaw depot, paid fifty cents for the rickshaw fee, and had one hundred and fifty cents left, both copper coins and copper tickets, all stuffed in his pocket. He bought a pack of cigarettes with five cents, put one in his mouth, and walked back slowly along the shade of the wall. His home was a large courtyard shared by ten families in a dozen or so rooms. The "large" in "large courtyard" did not praise the size of the house, but rather the chaotic nature of the courtyard. Besides the three rickshaw pullers, the families were mostly small craftsmen like shoemakers, cart drivers, and sugar figure makers. As soon as Zhang Xiaosan entered the courtyard, he saw his wife, Zhang Ersao, with a soapy washbasin on a square stool under the eaves, apparently intending to wash her face. He walked forward and kicked the stool over with his foot. The washbasin made a "clang" and water spilled all over the ground. Zhang Ersao, who was just about to go inside to get a white cloth towel, turned around and stamped her foot, saying, "Have you gone mad? What did the washbasin do to you?" Zhang Xiaosan tilted the cigarette in his mouth and scolded, "A rickshaw puller's wife, using foreign soap to wash her face? What are you trying to beautify yourself for? I, Zhang Xiaosan, don't sell wives for profit, so there's no need for you to be so extravagant. Or do you have your eye on some young, good-looking guy in this alley and want to seduce him?" Zhang Ersao had a yellowish persimmon face with a ponytail that reached her neck, but there were large strands of yellow hair on both sides that reached her ears. She wore a blue cloth jacket that resembled a Taoist robe, loose and not fitting her body. She tossed her head, and the stray hairs and ponytail swayed with her. Raising her arm, which exposed half of her yellowish-wax-colored arm, she pointed and said, "Zhang Xiaosan, are you talking like a human being? The poor should still have some dignity! It's not excessive to buy a piece of coarse soap for eight cents to wash my face. If you can't bear to spend a few cents, fine. I'll just grab a handful from the feces and urine and cook that for you to eat! Let me tell you, don't go crazy like this again. This old woman is like settling accounts while riding a donkey—just you wait and see!" Zhang Xiaosan threw the cigarette in his mouth on the ground, laughed, and said, "She's putting on airs! Zhang Xiaosan doesn't lack a clever wife like you. When I strike it rich, we'll..." "Bang!" The door slammed shut. Zhang Ersao said from inside the room, "Don't come in. Go get rich!" Zhang Xiaosan said, "Don't make trouble. I need to go in and get some clean clothes. I want to go to the bathhouse to take a bath." Zhang Ersao said, "Who's making trouble with you? Why don't you look at your face in the chamber pot? Do you even deserve it?"

A Journey Around the Yellow Sea (29) 231

— Huang Yanpei

Sixty Rhymes on a Journey to the Yellow Sea

In Liaoyang, the ice melts firmly in the third month. I followed the spring scenery out of the willow banks. Traveling by land is not as convenient as floating on the sea. I took a detour through Qingdao to Dalian. The flock of seagulls bid farewell to me with sincere thoughts. Recalling the seagulls, I wanted to tap on the side of the boat. The old fortress has been covered in insects and sand for fifteen years. Stroking it, the atmosphere is still enduring for thousands of years. The astronomical observatory has become a place to survey the vast cosmos. The wonders of heaven and earth are right before my eyes. A great thief enters the house, and the owner loses power. They seize treasures and flaunt them in the marketplace. What was unseen in the past is now seen. I tried the hot springs under the Qian Mountains. Temporarily cleansing my heart, I felt as light as a fairy. I went straight to Shenyang, shaking the reins of my horse while composing poetry. Good sons and good wives welcomed me with joy. The Grand Academy is green and pure. Morning meals and evening delicacies were accompanied by the sound of spring strings. Paintings entered the city in a winding procession. Zhongxuan's secretary was so elegant. The literary talents of Jiangshan were rich and vast. I widely collected literature to compile a great work, taking on the burden of the White Mountains and Black Waters. Among them, I especially admired the virtuous magistrate. Light carriage, simple entourage, walking through the streets. Da Han Ying Tun is an ancient legend. Xi Zhai visited his father and wept here. The people and the place are blessed by heaven. An official who loves the people and not money. Teaching the masses with simple words and clear principles. On the way back, I visited the ancient people's temple. The stone horses of Zhao Mausoleum are covered with green grass. I can't put down the blue and green thoughts. My ten days in Shenyang have not been wasted. The diligent students were eager to learn day and night. I am ashamed of lacking a broad and eloquent tongue. The ancient Korean name of the Mazhi River has been passed down. The names of Han Mountain and Han River still exist. Ink filled the tent above the Mingyue Tower. Entering the Qiting, the singing startled all around. The dragon head pines above the court were locked in smoke. I departed from Bakan at dusk and couldn't sleep. Cherry blossoms filled the fields like snow. Snowy skin and floral faces competed for spring beauty. The thunderous train flew across the Edo River. The spring city flower festival was filled with colorful carriages. Tokyo and Xijing followed one after another. The falling petals quickly turned into the sound of cuckoos. I floated on a painted boat on Lake Ashi and the West Sea. The cauldron at the Owakudani valley boiled fiercely. The four mountains were white, and the clouds spread out. I never had a half-face encounter with Mount Fuji. The mountain spirit and I stared at each other. My wife in her dark blue dress wore out her feet in vain. The blue sea chickens and pigs were deliciously fat. I returned to the ancient Kinkaku-ji Temple along winding paths. I packed up my travels and returned to my inkstone field. I completed this Yellow Sea Round-Trip Poem. (The End)

The rise and fall were only three or four taels. Yesterday, the 12th, the gold standard continued to decline slightly, with some fluctuations, hovering around 800 taels all day. Looking back, it has already fallen by 5 taels. The silver market reported an increase in the initial opening, then a slight decrease. Zhabei: Yesterday in the Northern Shanghai rice market, 3-4 barge numbers of rice boats were seen arriving from various routes. Sales continued to be extremely slow. Sales of Changshu and Xixi white japonica varied, with initial transactions being acceptable but prices weakening slightly. Medium-grade and lower rice prices weakened by 2 jiao. Early and late rice lacked customers, with more arriving, prices shrank by 3-4 jiao, changing to 2 yuan in the shade. Wine sales also turned sluggish. Bo rice with short quantity and a small amount of foreign currency sold slowly and demand in the markets are slowing, prices slightly softening. The trend for Lu Bu rice also remained lacking in spirit, with sales and arrivals each down by 2, shrinking by 1 chi. Sales of Southern Port white rice were better, the market surface was firm, and prices of guest rice had no major gains or losses. About 2600-2700 dan of various goods were opened from boats.

South Shanghai: Yesterday's rice situation saw over 20 boats arriving. Northern japonica sales were extremely dull, and prices fell by 2 jiao. Su Tongbei's white japonica also trended downstream, with the situation being poor. Sales in both urban and rural areas of the entire city were slow. Prices recovered by 1.5 chi. Bo rice and early rice from Nanbang, Shipu, Sijing, Songjiang, and other places saw the decline turn heavy, with a drop of 2-3 jiao. This was due to the lack of buying interest and arrivals, as well as soft prices in the production areas. Although the arrival of foreign rice was slightly scarcer, the accumulated rice remained unsold, and the appetite remained closed. This street remained insignificant, leading to a further decrease of 0.5 chi in prices. Glutinous rice and white rice sales also turned sluggish, with the situation trending downstream.

Wheat Flour: Prices Gradually Decrease 241

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning and afternoon, prices for all months trended downward. The quotation for foreign wheat also decreased by 1-2 jiao. The weather was also calm and sunny, exceptionally good. Both domestic and international environments favored short positions. The mentality of inland merchants also seemed to be inevitably influenced. They had no choice but to gradually sell off their long positions. Although the factories still maintained their positions, and merchants from Southeast Asia slightly increased their purchases, the overall trend was still downward. Recently, over 70% of the new wheat in the Jiangnan and Jiangbei regions has been harvested. Samples sent to Shanghai were all exceptionally dry. The quality in Jiangbei was also better than in previous years. The sluggishness of the market was beyond human control. As a result, the price for this month fell by 2.75 fen compared to the previous day, July fell by 2.5 fen, August fell by 1.5 fen, September fell by 1.75 fen, October fell by 1.25 fen, and November fell by 1.75 fen.

Wheat Futures All Extremely Weak 242

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning and afternoon, prices for all months trended sluggish and listless. The quotation for foreign wheat also decreased by 1-2 jiao, seemingly declining throughout the week. In addition, the weather was beautiful and sunny, as usual. With such favorable natural conditions, there was no way to prevent the price from falling. Therefore, although the long positions of the traders still tried to struggle, they softened due to the unfavorable environment. Given the good wheat harvest this year and the large factories still having foreign wheat as reserves, a surge of arrivals is expected, and the decline may be intensifying. As a result, the price for this month fell by 3 fen compared to the previous day, July fell by 5 fen, August, September, and October fell by 2 fen, and November fell by 1 fen. Regarding the new wheat situation, the arrival of cargo ships and boats has been surging in recent months. However, the factories' appetite has not been strong, and only limited quantities have been traded. Yesterday, 1,500 bags of Hezhou wheat were opened, priced at 3 taels and 9 qian, followed by 3 taels, 8 qian, and 7 fen.

Foreign Rice Sales Continue 243

Yesterday, the market conditions for customer rice were completely stagnant. Neither local nor outside customers inquired. The owners were also unwilling to lower prices to sell. There were still thousands of bags of rice stored in the market, but most of them were of medium or lower quality. The amount of high-quality rice in the hands of the four households was also very small. The foreign rice market was slightly active yesterday, but prices weakened. According to reports, 720 bags of Saigon No. 1 were sold by this street and merchants from the Yangtze River, priced at 11 yuan to 10 yuan and 9 jiao. 200 tons of small broken rice were priced at 5 taels and 6 fen, for delivery at the end of June. New transactions and orders have not yet been concluded because prices in the producing areas are high and the Shanghai market is weak, making it difficult to make a profit.

Silk and Tea: Most Wuxi Cocoon Businesses Suspend Weighing 244

Few Goods Available, Supply Can’t Meet Demand: Higher Prices for Superior Cocoons

This year, a total of over 130 cocoon businesses opened in the various markets and villages of Wuxi. However, the cocoon production was extremely poor, with only 27-28% of the usual harvest. It has only been 6-7 days since the weighing scales have opened, and the amount received by each business is only one-tenth to one-twelfth of that in previous years. The arrival of goods in the market is not strong, and businesses are competing to buy cocoons by increasing prices, leading to higher opening prices for superior cocoons, with a maximum of 85-86 yuan (improved variety of superior cocoons) and a minimum of 40 yuan (inferior native species). There are few goods and many businesses, making it impossible for supply to meet demand. In the past two days, there have been no more goods to collect. Most cocoon businesses in Qingcheng City, Tianxia City, Tianshang City, and Fu'an Township have suspended weighing. It is expected that the cocoon market in Xiyi will end this week.

Shanghai Factories Take the Opportunity to Cover Shorts as European Dealers Buy 245

Yesterday, the spot sales of raw silk in the Shanghai foreign dealer market remained stagnant. However, European dealers generally believed that the price of raw silk processed by Shanghai factories had fallen to the lowest limit. Due to the shrinking exchange rate overseas, the opening price increased. Therefore, they took the opportunity to cover their shortages. However, because the cost of silk for each manufacturer was not low, they insisted on selling at high prices, making it difficult for transactions to be smooth. Yesterday, only Dayi and others imported 20 bales of old raw silk processed by white silk factories in Shanghai, and Xinfu imported 15 bales of raw silk processed by yellow silk factories in Shandong. The prices were firm.

Ping Shui Green Tea Sells Well to America 246

Yesterday, tea businesses such as Xiehe, Jinlong, Dede, and Tianxiang in Huzhou's Pingshui Green Tea area all started searching for goods. The total number of transactions in the city reached over 5,000 boxes, and the market was lively. However, this type of tea has always been sold at wholesale prices by merchants from all over the country. This year, due to the poor harvest in the producing areas and the high prices from Chinese merchants, the major merchants have been unable to open. Currently, most merchants are buying in small quantities. Among them, pearl tea is priced at 85 to 100 taels, which is 20 to 30 taels higher than before. The prices for other items such as needle tea and precious eyebrow tea are also similar. As for Luzhuang's precious eyebrow green tea, goods from Tunxi and Wuyuan arrived in Shanghai yesterday, but the Chinese merchants were unwilling to lower prices to sell, and transactions remained sparse.

Piece Goods: Piece Goods Continue to Rise 247

The piece goods market is becoming more firm. Although the gold market fell slightly yesterday, people's hearts were somewhat limited. The three ports have rebounded, and Osaka's price for patterned goods is again 2.5 li higher. Therefore, Tianjin merchants have strong buying intentions. The volume of spot and futures transactions for Zhongbing Yuehua velvet Huxinting serge and other items exceeded 300 pieces. Merchants from Sichuan also expressed buying intentions. Yesterday, there was appetite from three to four department stores for fine serge. It was not easy to find spot goods, so prices only rose and did not fall. Sijunzi Zhigong wool has been sold for 3 qian and 2 fen. Sanyou Tu was completely bought up by Tianjin merchants, and the current futures price is 3 qian and 4 fen. Even blue corduroy and color corduroy are popular. The price of fine serge, Shiqiu Gucheng, and Ling was consistently 3 qian and 9.5 fen yesterday. Huxinting was sold out at 3 qian and 4 fen. The price of summer goods at the beginning of the yuan has not increased. White crepe has already shown a turnaround. Rengou Xu is priced at 4 taels and 2 qian, and Wuye Tishu and Magic City have all been cleared at 4 taels and 1 qian. Due to the excessive decline in printed white-ground satin, it has attracted the attention of speculators. The prices all need to be cleared for 2 qian, and the estimated cost, plus storage and interest, is quite reasonable. Therefore, even goods priced at 1 qian and 8 fen yesterday have disappeared.

Sugar Market: 300 Tons of Dumped Dutch Brown Sugar Surge 248

Yesterday's telegrams from the sugar market production areas: The current price of Cuban sugar is still 1.3125, the New York sugar futures price for September is 1.28, December is 1.37, March of next year is 1.44, and May is 1.50. Compared to the previous telegram, only December and May of next year have each risen by 1 point, and there have been no changes in other months. The current price of Javanese sugar and June futures are both 8 guilders, and July and August are 8.125, with little change compared to the previous period. The association's market transactions were very quiet, with both buying and selling sluggish. Dutch sugar No. 24 coarse granulated white was 11 taels and 5 qian, and No. 20 medium granulated white was 10 taels, 8 qian, and 5 fen. Transactions were very few. The Japanese sugar market also declined slightly. N Mark was 11 taels and 3 qian, J Mark was 11 taels, 7 qian, and 2.5 fen, SH Mark was 11 taels and 5 fen, YT Mark was 11 taels and 3 qian, YRO was 10 taels, 9 qian, and 5 fen, and TP Mark was 11 taels and 7 qian. The trend was stable. Throwing Goods: The Jicheng foreign firm sold 200 tons of Dutch brown sugar No. 8-9 loaded in July, August, and September, priced at 5 Dutch guilders. At the same time, Nan Chenglong also offered 100 tons at the same price. The market was not unusual. Huaxin offered 1,000 bags of spot coarse granulated white at 11 taels and 5 qian per bag, but the demand was not strong. The original amount of over 3,000 bags could not be sold out at once.

Social News

Marshal Foch's Diary of the European War 266

— Translated by Gu Angruo

"The Commanders-in-Chief of the British, French, and American forces continue to command their troops. If any Commander-in-Chief feels that General Foch's instructions are placing his troops in a dangerous position, he has the right to appeal to his home government."

Mr. Lloyd George came from London to attend, landed at Boulogne, and drove to Bommiers. Mr. Clemenceau had arrived earlier. On the way, Mr. George encountered retreating British troops. Seeing their poor morale and dispirited state, he knew the situation was unfavorable. Therefore, he arrived at the meeting with a disheartened impression, quite late.

However, he soon shook off this depressed demeanor and regained his characteristic energy. At the meeting, he declared to me: "The British people trust you. Your appointment as Commander-in-Chief of the Allied forces is unanimously welcomed in our country."

After the meeting, as we left the room, he said to me with his usual cheerful manner, "Now, I bet, who is it going to be? Ludendorff or Foch?" I calmly replied, "You must first back me, and then you will win. Because Ludendorff must break through our army, and he is now incapable of doing so. As for us, our current task is to stop him. We are very confident about this. Afterwards, when the time comes, we will break through him. That is another question. How far we can go will soon be seen."

The Bommiers Agreement could not fully accommodate my suggestions, and therefore failed to extend my authority to control the entire Western Front from the North Sea to the Adriatic Sea, or all Allied forces fighting there. However, it already contained the elements of commanding the French line of battle. The French line was the main theater of war, and the American, British, and French forces fighting there were also the main Allied forces. But Mr. Clemenceau, having now obtained the approval of the British and American governments for this new plan, certainly preferred to limit the authority of the Allied Commander-in-Chief to this theater and these three armies, pending the maturity of the opportunity. Once this result was achieved, he reserved the possibility of seeking future expansion of the agreement to include the Italian theater, on the one hand, and the Belgian forces, on the other, and the Italian forces.

The motion to include Italy was studied by the Supreme War Council on May 2nd at Abbeville. Mr. Orlando and Mr. Sonnino, on behalf of the Italian government, declared that they could not unconditionally agree to the Bommiers Agreement. However, for the sake of compromise, they proposed to distinguish between the command of the Italian line and the Italian army. This plan was agreed to by other governments and contained the following:

(1) The Italian line will henceforth be under the control of General Foch, according to the Doulens Agreement.

(2) As for the Italian army, it will only be under his control when other Allied forces arrive outside the Alps and fight under his command in a similar situation as in France.

This restriction by the Italian government still allowed the Allied Commander-in-Chief to inspect the Italian line and, when necessary, to implement his strategy, taking advantage of the possibility of crossing the Alpine war zone.

Regarding the Belgian forces, the Supreme War Council discussed this issue on July 3rd at Versailles. At that time, the Allied forces were preparing to launch an offensive in France. It was expected that the Belgian forces would participate in this battle, and it would be best to put them under my control, just like other Allied forces. However, Major General Gillain, Chief of Staff of the Belgian Army, formally opposed this proposal, citing the Belgian Constitution. As a result, no understanding could be reached.

In fact, this uncooperative attitude mostly arose on principle and was not immutable. A few weeks later, the King of Belgium did not hesitate to accept the task of directing the Belgian, French, British, and American Allied forces fighting in France, according to the Allied Commander-in-Chief's dispositions.

On May 2nd, the Allied governments decided to abolish the Executive Committee established three months earlier, as it was no longer necessary. On May 14th, I assumed the title of Commander-in-Chief of the Allied Forces in France.

But this was only a formal procedure to define my authority on paper. In practice, how this newly created Allied Commander-in-Chief would exercise his authority remained to be seen.

In early April 1918, the situation was still precarious. The front line was extended due to repeated enemy victories. Soldiers, exhausted and hoarse, had to reverse the declining trend. There was no more time for procrastination.

On his part, General Pétain advanced the Fifth Army along the Somme further north. This army, because it did not want to launch an offensive at that time, was replenished by drawing from the reserves. He also moved the Arras Army Group westward. This army group had two divisions, part of which advanced to the right bank of the Arras River. He further transferred the First Cavalry Corps from Andelys to Omer.

General Fayolle was ordered to immediately move the reserves on the left flank, in order to assist the British Fourth Army in the Lusem area in times of urgent need.

Finally, instructions were given to General Maistre, commander of the Tenth Army, to handle the military affairs in front of Arras. If the enemy attacked, the main line of defense must be firmly held with all strength. The operational steps were prescribed for him and the Third Army in the instructions. The initial deployment and the method of his participation in the war were also indicated to him.

When arranging for the French army to participate in the war between Arras and the Somme River, I also paid attention to doing my best to assist the British Commander-in-Chief, because he was unsettled by the material and spiritual difficulties of the Battle of Flanders. On the 12th, I decided to increase the reinforcements that had begun to be supplied to him two days earlier.

I ordered the reserve forces in the Omer area, the Second Cavalry Corps, to depart for Saint-Omer. After arriving on the 13th, they were prepared to join the French 133rd Division to reinforce the British Second Army.

General Robillot, commander of the Second Cavalry Corps, came to Sarcus (note: my headquarters had moved to Sarcus on April 7th, three miles northwest of Grandvilliers) to receive instructions. When instructing him on his operational tasks, I specifically instructed him to do his utmost to maintain contact between the British First and Second Armies.

The strategic outline is as follows:

(1) Fully support the two flanks of the gap, continuing to occupy the Kemmelberg-Mount Cassel line in the north, and continuing to occupy the Beaucourt-Saint-Amiens line in the south, to the northeast.

(2) Between these firmly held flanks, occupy key points to the east to prevent the enemy from advancing.

(To be continued)

Youth Garden

Fudan Drama Society Performance of "The Liar" 267

Date: Set for Today and Tomorrow

Location: Ningbo Native Place Association

Since the last performance of "Cyrano de Bergerac," the Fudan Drama Society has been preparing for its eleventh major performance. The play is the famous work "The Liar" by the British playwright Jones. It was performed once at Fudan University on the evening of the first of this month. It has now been decided to present a grand performance at the Ningbo Native Place Association today and tomorrow. This play has been adapted and translated by the Society, so it is very suitable for the national situation and has no defects of disharmony. In addition, the scenery design is magnificent and elegant, the plot of the play is humorous and witty, and the actors are carefully selected and are all rich in stage experience. It is heard that the ticket sales points are at the North Star, Guanghua, and Modern bookstores on the Fourth Road, and the seat prices are half a yuan and one yuan.

Fudan's "The Liar" 268

— Wu

"The theatrical atmosphere in Shanghai has been extremely quiet lately."

Everyone breathing in this metropolis of three million people feels this way. It's true, the Southern Country Drama Society has disintegrated, there is no news of the Drama Association rehearsing, the Xinyou Drama Troupe seems to have lost its energy since the so-called difficult drama movement, and the Modern Drama Society, which once worked hard to promote the mobile theater movement, has also gone back to their own dreams and stopped its work. However, various school drama societies, which had been active in succession during the so-called theatrical year of the 19th year of the Republic, have also declined and fallen into silence, following the craze of the publishing industry.

However, the theater groups in Shanghai have not all disappeared, have they? Aren't the newly established Qing'e Drama Society and Su Ni Drama Society preparing for public performances?

The Fudan Drama Society has made many contributions to the struggling Chinese theater scene with its ten consecutive performances, and last year it made a great effort to perform the great "Cyrano de Bergerac," which no Chinese troupe dared to perform and which required fifty or sixty people to be on stage. Now, they are gathering their spirits again and rehearsing their eleventh performance.

The play to be performed this time is "The Liar," a masterpiece by the great British playwright Jones. "The Liar" has been a sensation in the European and American theater circles in the past and has received a lot of good reviews.

The author loudly calls out in the play that it is not worth it for a person to sacrifice his honor, reputation, national responsibility, conscience, and everything else for the sake of a woman. In our country, there are quite a few people who abandon the dangers of the nation and the country because they are infatuated with women, and this should be a great wake-up call.

"The Liar," a comedy of life, satirizes the marriage disputes between men and women in England at that time and points the way for men and women who have lost their way. Now, Mr. Zhu Duanjun of the Society has adapted and translated it to suit the national situation of China.

The play tells the story of a wealthy businessman from Southeast Asia who happens to come to Shanghai for a visit and meets several married women, and falls into a furious tide of love with the most beautiful one. With this as the beginning, a story that is both humorous and witty, profound, and full of life's meaning unfolds.

Unexpectedly, that couple happened to meet at a hotel on the coast of Wusong, and happened to be seen by the younger brother of the woman's husband. How could this be? The crime of a secret meeting at the hotel was then added to their shoulders. From this misunderstanding, the third act, which is the most interesting and the most important part of the whole play, unfolds.

Helpless, they discussed with their relatives and friends how to hide it from their husband. Should they tell him the truth? That would only make things worse. It was decided to create a perfect lie. The lie agreed upon by a few people was gradually joined by most people. There were actually three male and three female characters who worked together to create the lie, reaching the most brilliant moment of the whole play. But unfortunately, because there were too many people involved, the lie that was expected to be perfect unintentionally revealed flaws, almost leading to an uncontrollable situation.

The story turns around here, from a couple who are about to break up to a path of rekindling their old love and ending. In the last act, there are a few famous lines that can be offered to the men and women who are living a miserable life in the air of divorce fever: "Don't think that you can neglect your wife after you get married. You can't. Now you have married the most beautiful woman in Shanghai, but if you don't continue to love her, someone else will love her. There's nothing to say, this is the tragedy of life."

In this play, there are six ladies on stage, breaking the record for the most female actors needed in previous performances by various theater groups. If the stage were changed to a domestic goods mall, some people might think it was a fashion exhibition. But it's not, they are all young women who love drama and are willing to work hard for it.

They, these few actresses, are the beautiful princesses in the Eastern Palace that people often praise. The most beautiful princesses are all gathered in this play. If it is necessary to introduce them in advance, it is also possible to say a little bit about them.

The first one to be mentioned is Ms. Liang Peishu. She has a talent for acting, needless to say, the subtlety of her expressions, the brightness of her lines, etc., have already been established. Originally, she played the female lead in the great Cyrano de Bergerac. This time, the passionate female lead is

Ms. Li Lian, she is right, her acting skills are very skilled, and her stage experience is extraordinary and abundant. She has played many roles, worthy of being a member trained by a famous director. There is also her sister,

Ms. Qin Quan, is also a talented actress in the new drama world. She doesn't care about the importance of the role, she is learning on the road to success. The one who needs a secluded and virtuous personality in this play is

Ms. Ouyang, she matches the personality in the play. She sings very well, and when she speaks her lines, it sounds like a clear warbling of birds.

The other ladies, I can't introduce them one by one. In short, they are all who have shown their talents in the spoken drama world. Because there are so many women in this play, the title of the play was once changed to "The Lying Women."

If you are looking forward to seeing these ladies and this clever plot, coincidentally, it will be performed at the Ningbo Native Place Association today. The performance says,

"The Liar" Leading Role Ms. Liang Peishu 269
